What is a branch of the theory of computation in theoretical computer science? Computational complexity theory<sep> What is a computational problem understood to be? a task that is in principle amenable to being solved by a computer<sep> What is equivalent to stating that the problem may be solved by mechanical application of mathematical steps, such as an algorithm? computational complexity theory<sep>
What is a problem regarded as inherently difficult if its solution requires significant resources, whatever the algorithm used<sep> The theory formalizes this intuition by introducing mathematical models of computation to study these problems and quantifying the amount of resources needed to solve them, such as time and storage<sep> What is used in communication complexity? number of gates in a circuit<sep> What is used in parallel computing? number of processors<sep> What is one of the roles of computational complexity theory? to determine the practical limits on what computers can and cannot do<sep>
What are closely related fields in theoretical computer science? analysis of algorithms and computability theory<sep> What is a key distinction between analysis of algorithms and computational complexity theory? the latter is devoted to analyzing the amount of resources needed by a particular algorithm to solve a problem<sep> What does the latter ask? what kind of problems can, in principle, be solved algorithmically<sep>
What can be viewed as an infinite collection of instances together with a solution for every instance? A computational problem<sep> What is the input string for a computational problem referred to as? a problem instance<sep> What can serve as the input for a decision problem? concrete utterance<sep>
What is the difference between a problem and an instance? the decision version of the traveling salesman problem<sep> What is the number of kilometers of route passing through all of Germany's 15 largest cities? 2000<sep> What does complexity theory address? computational problems and not particular problem instances<sep>
When considering computational problems, a problem instance is a string over an alphabet<sep> What is the binary alphabet? the set 0,1<sep> What are the strings? bitstrings<sep> What can be represented in binary notation? integers<sep> What can be encoded directly via their adjacency matrices, or by encoding their adjacency lists in binary? integers<sep>
What is one of the central objects of study in computational complexity theory? Decision problems<sep> What is a decision problem? a special type of computational problem whose answer is either yes or no, or alternately either 1 or 0.<sep> What is the objective of a decision problem? to decide, with the aid of an algorithm, whether a given input string is a member of the formal language under consideration<sep>
What is an example of a decision problem? an arbitrary graph<sep> What is the input of an arbitrary graph? The problem consists in deciding whether the given graph is connected, or not<sep> What is the formal language associated with the decision problem? the set of all connected graphs<sep>
What is a computational problem where a single output is expected for every input? function problem<sep> What is the output more complex than that of a decision problem? yes or no<sep> What are some examples of a function problem? traveling salesman problem and the integer factorization problem<sep>
The notion of function problems is much richer than the notion of what? decision problems<sep> Function problems can be recast as what? decision problems<sep> The multiplication of two integers can be expressed as the set of triples (a, b, c) so that the relation a  b = c holds<sep>
